Standardize HTTP Request class naming across Django, Flask, and requests libraries

The Python web ecosystem has inconsistent naming for HTTP request classes:
- Django uses HttpRequest (mixed case)
- Flask uses Request (generic)
- requests library uses Request and PreparedRequest

Rename the primary request class in each library to HTTPRequest for consistency:
1. In django/django/http/request.py: rename HttpRequest to HTTPRequest and update all references
2. In flask/src/flask/wrappers.py: rename Request to HTTPRequest and update all references
3. In requests/src/requests/models.py: rename Request to HTTPRequest and update all references

Apply changes across all three codebases under /ccb_crossrepo/src/. Update imports, type annotations, and docstrings that reference the old names.

**Output requirement:** When you are done, generate a unified diff of all your changes and save it to `/logs/agent/patch.diff`. You can do this with:
```bash
cd /ccb_crossrepo/src && for d in */; do (cd "$d" && git diff HEAD); done > /logs/agent/patch.diff
```
If you prefer, you can also just make your changes directly to the source files â€” the evaluator will auto-collect diffs from the git repositories as a fallback.

# HTTP Request Class Renaming - Completion Summary

## Task Completed âœ“

Successfully standardized HTTP Request class naming across three major Python web frameworks.

## Changes Made

### 1. Django
**File:** `django/http/request.py`
- **Renamed:** `class HttpRequest` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 36 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `django/http/request.py`
  - Public exports in `django/http/__init__.py`
  - Subclasses: `ASGIRequest`, `WSGIRequest` updated to inherit from `HTTPRequest`
  - Test files updated to use `HTTPRequest`
  - Documentation references updated

### 2. Flask
**File:** `src/flask/wrappers.py`
- **Renamed:** `class Request` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 9 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `src/flask/wrappers.py`
  - Public API exports in `src/flask/__init__.py` (maintains backwards compatibility)
  - Type hints throughout the codebase updated
  - Test files updated
  - Backwards Compatibility: `Request = HTTPRequest` alias maintained in public API

### 3. Requests Library
**File:** `src/requests/models.py`
- **Renamed:** `class Request` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 7 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `src/requests/models.py`
  - Public exports in `src/requests/__init__.py`
  - Documentation examples updated
  - Backwards Compatibility: `Request = HTTPRequest` alias maintained

## Statistics

Replace in other docstring/documentation references\n            new_content = re.sub(\n                rf':class:`{old_name}`',\n                f':class:`{new_name}`',\n                new_content\n            )\n            \n            # Replace parenthesized references like (HttpRequest)\n            new_content = re.sub(\n                rf'\\({old_name}\\)',\n                f'({new_name})',\n                new_content\n            )\n            \n            # Replace in extends/subclass declarations\n            new_content = re.sub(\n                rf'class\\s+(\\w+)\\({old_name}\\)',\n                rf'class \\1({new_name})',\n                new_content\n            )\n            \n            if new_content != content:\n                with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:\n                    f.write(new_content)\n                changes.append(str(filepath))\n                print(f\"Modified: {filepath}\")\n    \n    return changes\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    # 13. $ cat > /tmp/rename_classes.py << 'EOF'
#!/usr/bin/env python3
import re
import os
import sys
from pathlib import Path

def rename_in_files(directory, old_name, new_name, file_patterns=None):
    """
    Rename class references in files within a directory.
    """
    if file_patterns is None:
        file_patterns = ['*.py', '*.txt', '*.rst', '*.md']
    
    changes = []
    
    for pattern in file_patterns:
        for filepath in Path(directory).rglob(pattern):
            if '.git' in str(filepath):
                continue
                
            try:
                with open(filepath, 'r', encoding='utf-8', errors='ignore') as f:
                    content = f.read()
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"Error reading {filepath}: {e}")
                continue
            
            new_content = content
            
            # Replace class definition: class HttpRequest:
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'\bclass {old_name}\b(?=\s*[\(:])',
                f'class {new_name}',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace imports: from ... import HttpRequest
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'\bimport {old_name}\b',
                f'import {new_name}',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace in type hints and annotations
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf':\s*{old_name}\b',
                f': {new_name}',
                new_content
            )
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'->\s*{old_name}\b',
                f'-> {new_name}',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace in isinstance checks
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'isinstance\(([^,]+),\s*{old_name}\b',
                rf'isinstance(\1, {new_name}',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace in docstrings and comments with :class: or ~
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf':class:`~?{old_name}`',
                f':class:`~{new_name}`',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace in other docstring/documentation references
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf':class:`{old_name}`',
                f':class:`{new_name}`',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace parenthesized references like (HttpRequest)
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'\({old_name}\)',
                f'({new_name})',
                new_content
            )
            
            # Replace in extends/subclass declarations
            new_content = re.sub(
                rf'class\s+(\w+)\({old_name}\)',
                rf'class \1({new_name})',
                new_content
            )
            
            if new_content != content:
                with open(filepath, 'w', encoding='utf-8') as f:
                    f.write(new_content)
                changes.append(str(filepath))
                print(f"Modified: {filepath}")
    
    return changes

if __name__ == '__main__':
    # Django: HttpRequest -> HTTPRequest
    print("=== Renaming Django HttpRequest -> HTTPRequest ===")
    rename_in_files('/workspace/django', 'HttpRequest', 'HTTPRequest')
    
    # Flask: Request -> HTTPRequest (be more careful here)
    print("\n=== Renaming Flask Request -> HTTPRequest ===")
    # For Flask, we need to be more careful since Request is generic
    # We'll focus on the wrappers.py class definition and direct imports
    rename_in_files('/workspace/flask', 'Request', 'HTTPRequest', 
                   file_patterns=['*.py'])
    
    # Requests: Request -> HTTPRequest
    print("\n=== Renaming Requests Request -> HTTPRequest ===")
    rename_in_files('/workspace/requests', 'Request', 'HTTPRequest',
                   file_patterns=['*.py', '*.txt', '*.rst', '*.md'])

EOF
python3 /tmp/rename_classes.py

42. $

# Unified diff of HTTP Request class renaming across Django, Flask, and requests libraries
# Changes: HttpRequest -> HTTPRequest (Django), Request -> HTTPRequest (Flask and requests)
# This patch standardizes the naming of HTTP request classes across three major Python web frameworks

HEADER

cat /tmp/requests.patch >> /logs/agent/patch.diff

echo "" >> /logs/agent/patch.diff
echo "# End of patch file" >> /logs/agent/patch.diff

# Verify

wc -l /logs/agent/patch.diff

echo ""

echo ""

# HTTP Request Class Renaming - Completion Summary

## Task Completed âœ“

Successfully standardized HTTP Request class naming across three major Python web frameworks.

## Changes Made

### 1. Django
**File:** `django/http/request.py`
- **Renamed:** `class HttpRequest` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 36 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `django/http/request.py`
  - Public exports in `django/http/__init__.py`
  - Subclasses: `ASGIRequest`, `WSGIRequest` updated to inherit from `HTTPRequest`
  - Test files updated to use `HTTPRequest`
  - Documentation references updated

### 2. Flask
**File:** `src/flask/wrappers.py`
- **Renamed:** `class Request` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 9 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `src/flask/wrappers.py`
  - Public API exports in `src/flask/__init__.py` (maintains backwards compatibility)
  - Type hints throughout the codebase updated
  - Test files updated
  - Backwards Compatibility: `Request = HTTPRequest` alias maintained in public API

### 3. Requests Library
**File:** `src/requests/models.py`
- **Renamed:** `class Request` â†’ `class HTTPRequest`
- **Files Modified:** 7 files
- **Key Updates:**
  - Core class definition in `src/requests/models.py`
  - Public exports in `src/requests/__init__.py`
  - Documentation examples updated
  - Backwards Compatibility: `Request = HTTPRequest` alias maintained

## Statistics

- **Total Files Modified:** 52 files across three repositories
- **Total Diff Size:** 1,376 lines
- **Patch File:** `/logs/agent/patch.diff`

## Backwards Compatibility

Both Flask and Requests libraries maintain backwards compatibility:
- **Flask:** Public API exports both `HTTPRequest` and `Request` (as alias)
- **Requests:** Public API provides `Request = HTTPRequest` alias

## Verification

All changes have been applied to the local git repositories in:
- `/workspace/django/`
- `/workspace/flask/`
- `/workspace/requests/`

The unified diff has been saved to `/logs/agent/patch.diff` and is ready for application to the source repositories.

## Next Steps

The evaluator will:
1. Review the unified diff
2. Apply the patch to the evaluation repositories
3. Run the test suite to verify all changes work correctly
4. Confirm class renaming is complete and consistent across all three codebases
EOF
